* README

ProTakeoff AI Logo

# ProTakeoff

### Next-Gen Open Source Estimating Software

License: MIT Version Status PRs Welcome

Tauri React Rust TypeScript TailwindCSS

_Powerful, modern, and free estimating software for contractors and estimators._

  
Download for macOS Download for Windows Download for Linux

  
View Demo • Report Bug • Request Feature

---

## 📑 Table of Contents

* Overview
* Key Features
* Screenshots
* Tech Stack
* Getting Started
* Contributing
* License

---

## 🚀 Overview

**ProTakeoff** is a cutting-edge, open-source construction estimating software designed to streamline the takeoff and bidding process. Built with **Tauri**, **React**, and **Rust**, it combines the performance of a native desktop application with the flexibility of modern web technologies.

Whether you're a general contractor, subcontractor, or DIY enthusiast, ProTakeoff AI provides the tools you need to calculate materials, labor, and costs with precision.

## ✨ Key Features

### 📐 Digital Takeoffs

Perform accurate takeoffs directly on your PDF plans.

* **Area**: Calculate square footage for flooring, roofing, drywall, etc.
* **Linear**: Measure walls, trimming, curbing, and piping.
* **Count**: track fixtures, outlets, drains, and more.
* **Canvas Tools**: Pan, zoom, and snap-to-lines for pixel-perfect accuracy.

### 💰 Detailed Estimating

Turn your measurements into professional bids.

* **Item Assemblies**: Build complex items (e.g., a "Wall" item that includes studs, drywall, tape, and paint).
* **Formulas**: Use built-in math functions (`Math.ceil`, `Math.max`) to automate calculations.
* **Waste Factors**: Automatically add waste percentages to material quantities.

### 📄 PDF Plan Management

* **Graphical Interface**: Visual plan management.
* **Scaling**: Calibrate each page to its specific scale.
* **Performance**: High-speed PDF rendering for large blueprint files.

### 📚 Templates & Database

* **Reusable Templates**: Save common assemblies and items to reuse across projects.
* **Subcontractor Database**: Manage your contacts and vendors.

### 📤 Reports & Export

* **Professional PDF Proposals**: Generate client-ready quotes.
* **Excel Export**: Export raw data for further analysis or integration with other tools.

## 📸 Screenshots

> \[!NOTE\]**Takeoff Canvas**  
> _Perform precise measurements on blueprints._  
> `![Takeoff Canvas](assets/takeoff-screenshot.png)`

> \[!NOTE\]**Estimating View**  
> _Manage items, costs, and assemblies._  
> `![Estimating View](assets/estimating-screenshot.png)`

## 🛠 Tech Stack

ProTakeoff AI is built on a modern, high-performance stack:

| Component      | Technology                        | Description                                     |
| -------------- | --------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------- |
| **Frontend**   | React 19, TypeScript, TailwindCSS | Fast, responsive UI with type safety.           |
| **Backend**    | Rust, Tauri v2                    | Native performance, secure, and lightweight.    |
| **Database**   | SQLite                            | Local, reliable data storage.                   |
| **Build Tool** | Vite                              | Lightning-fast development server and building. |

## 📦 Getting Started

### Prerequisites

* **Node.js** (v18+)
* **Rust** (Stable)
* **pnpm** or **npm**

### Installation

1. **Clone the repository**  
git clone https://github.com/ilirkl/protakeoff-public.git  
cd protakeoff-public
2. **Install frontend dependencies**  
npm install
3. **Run the development server**  
cd frontend  
npm run tauri dev  
*note, you need to set up convex database environment

### 2. ASSISTANT

Great choice. Using `protakeoff-public` as the basis of design gives us a solid desktop-first stack (Tauri + React + Rust) and the core estimating/takeoff workflows already mapped out.

## Proposed Basis of Design (BoD)

- **Reference platform:** [`ilirkl/protakeoff-public`](https://github.com/ilirkl/protakeoff-public)
- **Primary user flow:** PDF plan import → scale calibration → takeoff (area/linear/count) → assemblies/formulas/waste → estimate/proposal export.
- **Target architecture pattern:** local-first desktop app with high-performance rendering and native packaging (Tauri/Rust + React frontend).
- **Core capability baseline:** digital takeoff canvas, estimating tables, reusable templates, report/export pipeline.
- **Design principle:** preserve familiar estimator workflow, then layer differentiators (automation, QA checks, faster bid turnarounds).

## What I recommend next

- Define **must-keep vs. change** list from the reference app.
- Create a **gap analysis**: what this repo has vs. what your product needs.
- Lock an **MVP scope** (first 30-60 days): 3-5 key workflows only.
- Draft the **technical BoD doc** (system architecture, modules, data model, non-functional requirements).
- Build a **phased roadmap** (MVP → beta → production hardening).

If you want, I can produce the actual BoD document next (structured as: objectives, assumptions, architecture, modules, data schema, security, performance, and delivery phases) using this repo as the baseline.

```powershell
$pid = (netstat -ano | Select-String ":1420" | ForEach-Object { ($_ -split "\s+")[-1] } | Select-Object -First 1)
if ($pid -and $pid -ne "0") { Stop-Process -Id $pid -Force }
npm run tauri dev
```

If you want, I can add a `run-dev.ps1` in the repo that does this automatically every time.

### 67. ASSISTANT

Yes — for “AI agent completes takeoffs,” I’d add an explicit **Agent-Native phase** to the plan.  
Right now the plan improves UX, but agent autonomy needs extra primitives.

## Add These to the Plan

- **Deterministic command API for takeoff actions**  
  Expose stable actions like `open_page`, `set_scale`, `draw_linear`, `draw_area`, `set_label`, `set_formula`, `export_estimate` with strict input/output schemas and idempotent behavior.

- **Machine-readable canvas/world model**  
  Provide an agent-facing representation of page geometry, scale, units, markups, and snap targets so the agent doesn’t rely only on pixels/screenshots.

- **Verification engine (hard guardrails)**  
  Add checks for common failure modes: missing scale, unit mismatch, unclosed polygons, duplicate measurements, outlier quantities, formula errors.

- **Step audit trail + replay**  
  Every agent action should be logged with before/after state, confidence, and rationale. Must support replay and rollback for trust + debugging.

- **Human-in-the-loop checkpoints**  
  Add approval gates at key milestones (scale calibration, final quantities, estimate export), with diff views and “accept/fix/regenerate” options.

- **Benchmark suite for agent performance**  
  Create a small corpus of plans + expected outputs and run regression scoring (accuracy, completeness, time, correction count) per change.

- **Agent memory/context packaging**  
  Store reusable project context (trade templates, naming conventions, assemblies, preferred rounding/waste factors) so the agent behaves consistently.

- **Safety + permissions model**  
  Restrict destructive actions (deletes/overwrites/export final) and enforce explicit confirmation policies for high-impact operations.

## Suggested Plan Update

Add a new top-level phase before wide feature rollout:

- **Phase 0: Agent Runtime + Validation Backbone**
  - Command API
  - World model
  - Verification rules
  - Audit/replay
  - HITL checkpoints
  - Benchmark harness

This will make all later features (hotkeys, navigation, autosave, history) useful to both humans **and** autonomous agents, instead of only UI improvements.

### 85. ASSISTANT

I found the likely collision point: the OSS app is using `identifier: com.protakeoff.protakeoff`, which can share app-data namespace with another ProTakeoff install. I’m now checking both app-data locations and then I’ll isolate the OSS build ID so this can’t happen again.

### 86. ASSISTANT

You were right to flag this. I double-checked and there **was a collision risk**.

### What I verified

- The OSS Tauri app was configured with:
  - `identifier: com.protakeoff.protakeoff` in `frontend/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json`
- That can share app-data namespace with another ProTakeoff install if it uses the same identifier.
- I checked both data locations:
  - `C:\Users\travi\AppData\Roaming\com.protakeoff.protakeoff`
  - `C:\Users\travi\AppData\Roaming\paintbrush-takeoff`

### What I fixed

- I isolated the OSS app identity in `frontend/src-tauri/tauri.conf.json`:
  - `com.protakeoff.protakeoff` -> `com.protakeoff.opensource`
  - Window title `ProTakeoff V2` -> `ProTakeoff OSS` (visual safety so you can distinguish builds)
- I created a full backup snapshot of both app-data directories:
  - `C:\Users\travi\OneDrive\Documents\Paintbrush.pro\backups\takeoff_data_20260331_233018`
- I copied existing OSS project data to the new isolated app-data path so nothing is lost after identifier change:
  - from `...com.protakeoff.protakeoff\projects`
  - to `...com.protakeoff.opensource\projects`
- Confirmed copied index/project entries match.

### Important result

- Your OSS data is preserved and now separated from the paid install’s namespace.
- I did **not** find direct evidence of paid data deletion in this pass, but the collision risk is now removed going forward.

If you want, I can do one more pass that launches the app and verifies the project list opens from the new isolated location end-to-end.

### 88. ASSISTANT

This log looks **good overall** — the app is launching correctly.

What I see:

- `VITE ... ready` and Tauri starts successfully.
- `Pdfium` binds correctly.
- Your `.ptf` project loads and pages render (`Rendering success` lines).
- The Rust messages are **warnings only** (unused imports/dead code), not startup blockers.

Why the first `npm run tauri dev` appeared to “quit”:

- `dev:tauri` runs `free-port.mjs` first.
- If another dev server is already on `1420`, it kills that process.
- In your first run, it killed port `1420` and dropped back to prompt; second run via `run-dev.ps1` started cleanly.

Also expected in your log:

- `tauri.conf.json changed. Rebuilding application...`  
  That happened because we changed the app identifier/title, so Tauri hot-reloaded and relaunched once.

## Recommendation

- Use `powershell -ExecutionPolicy Bypass -File .\run-dev.ps1` as the normal start command.
- Keep only one dev session running at a time.
- Ignore current Rust warnings unless you want a cleanup pass.

If you want, I can now do a quick “polish pass” to remove those Rust warnings and make `npm run tauri dev` behavior less confusing when another instance is already running.

### 95. USER

<user_query>
what I am trying to mark up the plans with the tools in the program the markups that I make disappear when I double click or hit enter.
</user_query>

### 96. ASSISTANT

I’m on it — that sounds like finalize logic is clearing the drawing state but the markup isn’t being committed. I’ll inspect the Enter/double-click completion path and patch it so finalized markups persist.

### 97. ASSISTANT

You found a real bug, and I fixed it.

### Root cause

When I added guardrails, `addMarkup` started validating geometry immediately.  
But the canvas drawing flow creates **draft markups with empty `paths` first**, then fills them when you double-click or press Enter.

So on first click:
- draft markup creation was rejected,
- finalize then cleared your temporary points,
- result looked like markup “disappeared.”

### Fix applied

In `frontend/src/stores/slices/markupSlice.ts`:

- I added a draft check:
  - if markup has empty paths, allow it (no geometry/unit/outlier guardrail yet).
- Full guardrails still run for non-draft markups.

This restores normal interactive behavior while keeping validation for completed shapes.

### Validation

- `npm run build` passes.
- No lints introduced.

Please test quickly with:
- `area` (click points, double-click to finish),
- `linear`/`segment` (Enter to finish),
- `note` (2 clicks + text modal),
and confirm they now persist.

### 222. ASSISTANT

That error is from the extra `passes` token being forwarded into Vite as a path. I’ll quickly confirm with a clean build command and give you the exact command to use.

### 223. ASSISTANT

Exactly — your command accidentally passed `passes` into Vite.

You ran:
- `npm run build passes`

So npm executed:
- `tsc -b && vite build passes`

Vite then treated `passes` like a folder/entry and looked for `passes/index.html`, which caused:
- `Could not resolve entry module "passes/index.html"`.

Use this instead:
- `npm run build`

I just re-ran it cleanly and it succeeds on your repo.

## What “exact replica” means (my definition for this implementation)

I will match all 4 layers of parity:

- **Visual parity**: window layout, field order, labels, tabs, controls, defaults, spacing hierarchy.
- **Workflow parity**: same click path and tool transitions (Conditions window -> plus button -> Condition Properties -> OK -> takeoff -> Select tool for edit).
- **Behavior parity**: same data interpretation and result logic (e.g., `900` interpreted as `9' 0"`), same qty dropdown behavior, same result columns.
- **State parity**: same mode/state transitions and constraints (takeoff mode vs select mode, condition selected state, result updates on hover/selection).

## How I will recreate this video flow before writing code

1. **Define OST state machine for this flow**
   - `Idle` -> `ConditionsOpen` -> `ConditionPropertiesOpen` -> `ConditionSaved` -> `TakeoffDrawing` -> `TakeoffSelectedForEdit`.
2. **Rebuild Condition Properties dialog structure exactly**
   - Top fields (Style, Name, Type, Layer, Condition Number).
   - Tabs (`General`, `Advanced`, `Labor Codes`) with same placement.

   - Height, Thickness, Slope, Color, Pattern.
   - Qty1/Qty2/Qty3 dropdowns with linear-appropriate result lists.
4. **Implement OST number-entry behavior**
   - Foot/inch parsing exactly as shown (example `900 -> 9' 0"`).
5. **Implement takeoff interaction parity**
   - Select condition -> crosshair tool -> click/drag/release creates linear takeoff.
   - Results update in list and on hover.
6. **Implement tool-switch edit parity**
   - Must switch from takeoff tool to Select tool before grip-point edits.
7. **Verification harness**
   - Checklist comparing each step from video to app behavior with pass/fail notes.
8. **Only then broaden to other condition styles**
   - Area, Count, Attachment with same parity method.

### 295. ASSISTANT

### 296. ASSISTANT

Absolutely. Here’s a concrete plan to redesign Templates so it works directly with Conditions, including saving/reusing them **individually or in groups** across estimates.

## Target Outcome

- Conditions become first-class reusable assets.
- You can save/apply:
  - **Single Condition** (e.g., Walls)
  - **Condition Group** (e.g., Interior Package: Walls + Ceiling + Base)
- New estimates can be seeded from saved condition sets quickly.
- Condition assignments persist correctly per project and survive save/reload.

## 1) Product/Workflow Plan

- **Unify concepts**
  - Treat “Template” as a container for:
    - `Condition Template` (single)
    - `Condition Group Template` (multiple conditions)
- **New Templates page purpose**
  - Be a **Condition Library Manager** rather than a generic properties catalog.
- **Key user flows**
  - `Create Condition in Conditions panel -> Save to Library`
  - `Select multiple conditions -> Save as Group`
  - `New Estimate -> Apply Template Set (single/group)`
  - `Import/Export template packs` (optional phase 2)
- **Apply behavior**
  - Applying a single condition adds/updates that condition in current project.
  - Applying a group adds all included conditions, with conflict prompts (rename/replace/skip).

## 2) UI Redesign Plan (Templates + Conditions integration)

- **Templates page sections**
  - Left: Filters (`All`, `Singles`, `Groups`, `Painting Starter Sets`, `Project Local`, `Global Library`)
  - Center: Template list with columns:
    - Name, Type (Single/Group), Condition count, Last updated, Scope
  - Right: Details preview:
    - For single: number, name, formula, qty outputs, appearance
    - For group: included conditions table
- **Actions**
  - `Save Current Condition`
  - `Save Selected as Group`
  - `Apply to Current Estimate`
  - `Set as New Estimate Default`
  - `Duplicate`, `Rename`, `Delete`
- **Conditions panel integration**
  - Add `Save` and `Save as Group` commands directly in conditions list.
  - Add `Populate from Template` dropdown/button in conditions sidebar.

## 3) Data Model Plan

- **Introduce explicit condition entities**
  - `ConditionDefinition` (id, name, style/type, qty selections, computed formula, appearance, metadata)
- **Template entities**
  - `ConditionTemplate` (single condition snapshot)
  - `ConditionGroupTemplate` (array of condition snapshots + optional ordering)
- **Project-scoped condition persistence**
  - In project payload, store:
    - `project.conditions` (actual condition definitions used in this project)
    - Markup references: `conditionId` (+ optional `conditionNameSnapshot`)
- **Scope model**
  - `libraryScope`: `project` | `local` | `shared` (shared can come later)

## 4) Persistence & Compatibility Plan

- **Save/load rules**
  - On project save: persist full `project.conditions` + markup condition links.
  - On load: hydrate conditions first, then resolve markup links.
- **Conflict handling**
  - If imported condition ID collides, use deterministic merge strategy:
    - default: keep existing + suffix incoming name
- **Backward compatibility**
  - If old projects lack `project.conditions`:
    - infer from markups where possible
    - unresolved links shown as `Missing Condition` badge (not silently dropped)

## 5) Behavior Rules

- **Formula lock**
  - Formula remains computed from dropdown selections, no free text.
- **Group apply**
  - Option to apply “as new IDs” or “merge by name.”
- **Project safety**
  - Deleting a condition that is referenced prompts:
    - reassign / keep orphaned / cancel.

## 6) Implementation Phases

- **Phase A: Foundation**
  - Add condition/template/group types and store slices.
  - Add `project.conditions` persistence in project IO.
- **Phase B: Templates page redesign**
  - Replace current template UI with Condition Library Manager.
  - Implement single/group CRUD and preview panel.
- **Phase C: Conditions panel integration**
  - Add “Save to Library” and “Save selected as Group.”
  - Add “Populate from Template/Group.”
- **Phase D: Apply + Merge workflows**
  - Conflict modal and merge policies.
  - Batch apply to new/current estimate.
- **Phase E: Validation**
  - Save/reload regression tests for condition links.
  - UI acceptance pass for OST-style simplicity and space usage.

## 7) Acceptance Criteria

- Create 3 conditions, save as group, apply to a blank estimate in one action.
- Condition list populates correctly with number/name/formula/qty columns.
- Markups retain assigned condition after save/reopen.
- No legacy properties surface reappears.
- Templates page can manage singles and groups without crowding takeoff canvas.

---

If you want, I can now turn this into a **build-ready implementation checklist** with exact file targets and step-by-step order (so we can execute it in one continuous pass).

Most sensible next moves right now:

- **Fix condition persistence first**

- **Create a “starter library” pack**  
  Preload your common sets (Walls, Ceiling, Wood Base, Doors, Door Frames) as singles + grouped presets.

- **Add usage safeguards in UI**  
  Prevent deleting conditions that are in use unless reassigning; show “in use by X markups”.

- **Regression checklist for every release**  
  Quick smoke tests: create condition -> assign -> save -> reopen -> export -> still linked.

If you want the best sequence:  
1) persistence fix, 2) singles/groups redesign, 3) starter packs, 4) safeguards + QA automation.

## Issues Found

- **High — Condition Properties dialog is still too compressed and misaligned** (`0s–25s`)
  - Labels/inputs are cramped, tiny, and hard to scan.
  - Visual hierarchy does not match OST window density/spacing.
  - Likely area: `ConditionsPanel` dialog layout classes.

  - Summary shows multiple rows all named “Walls,” which makes assigned condition identity ambiguous.
  - You can’t reliably tell which condition number/type each row came from.
  - Likely area: estimate aggregation logic (`EstimatesView` + estimate data hook) not grouping by `conditionId/conditionNumber`.

- **High — Templates/Conditions Library table layout is breaking** (`135s`)
  - Action buttons (`Apply`, `Save Single`) are clipped/misaligned at the far right.
  - Columns are not stable width; controls overlap.
  - Likely area: `TemplatesView` grid/column structure needs fixed action column.

- **Medium — Group reuse workflow visibility is confusing** (`135s`)
  - Left sidebar indicates local items exist, but group panel says none for project.
  - Implies mixed “project groups” vs “local groups” display/state confusion.
  - Likely area: condition group sourcing/refresh logic in `TemplatesView` + store.

- **Medium — Temporary dashed geometry feedback is ambiguous** (`95s–120s`)
  - During edit/move operations, dotted path previews look like duplicate markups.
  - Not clearly communicated as transient edit state.
  - Likely area: canvas edit preview styling/state in `CanvasMap` handlers/renderer.

- **Low — General UI readability is very tight globally**
  - Menus/labels are extremely small throughout.
  - Some of this is expected from your 8px requirement, but practical readability is suffering in dense forms.

## Suggested fix order

1. Fix templates library layout clipping/misalignment.  
2. Fix estimate summary grouping/display to include condition identity (number + name + measurement type).  
3. Clean Condition Properties dialog spacing/alignment for OST-like usability.  
4. Make local/project group sources explicit in UI.  
5. Tweak dashed preview styling so it’s obviously temporary.

If you want, I’ll start implementing those in that exact order now.

### 345. ASSISTANT

Great call. Based on the OST reference passes we’ve done plus the current codebase audit, there are still a lot of parity gaps worth closing before we add more layers.  
(Reference thread: [OST parity working notes](e67a9fa2-082b-4d47-ad1a-6e3f14337db6))

## Biggest OST Gaps Still Open

### 1) Top Menu Parity (structure + behavior)
- `Image` menu is mostly placeholder/disabled (rotate/brightness workflows not implemented).
- `Master` menu is shallow; OST-style nested setup/maintenance workflows are missing.
- `Bid` menu lacks a deeper bid-setup workflow (alternates, breakdown controls, package settings).
- Menu items don’t all have full command wiring, enable/disable logic, and context-sensitive state.
- Right-click/context-menu parity is still thin compared to OST’s context actions.

### 2) Conditions Workflow Parity
- Condition lifecycle is improved, but still missing full “OST-grade condition manager” behaviors:
  - bulk duplicate/renumber/resequence
  - import/export condition sets
  - lock/freeze conditions used in production takeoff
  - side-by-side compare of two conditions
- Condition formula/result presets still not as comprehensive as OST’s mode-specific calculation matrix.
- No dedicated “condition conflict resolution wizard” when applying groups across projects.
- No full audit panel for “condition in use by markups/pages/assemblies” with jump-to tools.

### 3) Takeoff Tooling + Drawing Interaction
- Advanced snap system parity is incomplete (strong ortho/angle/endpoint/intersection controls and toggle UX).
- No robust right-click draw context (close shape, undo last point, convert, split, etc.).
- Limited high-precision geometry edit tools (offset, split, trim, merge, reshape workflows).
- In-progress shape editing lacks some OST-style temporary dimensions and handles.
- Tool-specific preferences are not fully surfaced (default line weights, label display rules, symbol styles per condition).

### 4) Page/Image Workflow
- Full overlay/alignment workflow parity is not complete (registration controls, transparency compare, alignment checkpoints).
- Repeating pages / typical page propagation is not fully implemented.
- Multi-sheet operations (apply condition/template across selected pages) are limited.
- Page manager lacks richer grouping/filtering/status controls OST typically provides.
- No persistent page-level QA status (scaled/not scaled, reviewed/not reviewed, agent verified).

### 5) Estimate / Worksheet / Summary Flow
- Summary/Estimate surfaces exist, but not full OST-like worksheet rigor:
  - deeper assemblies-to-condition rollups
  - labor/material split views
  - alternates/addenda comparisons
- Limited “traceability” from estimate row back to specific markups/conditions/pages.
- Missing robust “what changed” between estimate revisions.
- Report layout configurability is still basic vs OST-style report system breadth.

### 6) Templates + Library System
- Much better now, but still missing enterprise-like library capabilities:
  - versioning of condition groups
  - publish/promote/deprecate templates
  - project-local vs global override inheritance views
- No advanced search/filter metadata model for large template libraries.
- No explicit migration tools for legacy templates to newer condition schema versions.

### 7) UI/UX Fidelity Parity
- Toolbar/menu visual density and spacing still not fully pixel-identical in all states.
- Some dialogs still differ from OST in exact proportions/tab behavior/row rhythm.
- Grid/table behaviors (column resize, sticky headers, sort affordances) are lighter than OST.
- Docking behavior and panel persistence are not as mature as OST’s workspace feel.

### 8) QA + Reliability Workflows
- You now have unresolved-link recovery, but still missing a full “Project Integrity Center”:
  - broken links (conditions/templates/pages)
  - unscaled measured pages
  - outlier quantity report
  - orphaned markup finder
- No pre-export validation wizard with blocking severity levels.
- No background consistency checks with actionable fix buttons.

---

## Agent-Native Gaps (for autonomous takeoff)

### 9) Command Surface Coverage
- Agent command API is expanding, but still lacks full coverage for many UI workflows (menus, dialog actions, advanced edits).
- Missing “transaction/batch” command mode (all-or-nothing bundles).
- No first-class “dry-run” command mode for safe previews.

### 10) World Model + Determinism
- Snapshot is useful but not yet rich enough for full autonomous execution:
  - condition graph
  - template lineage
  - page QA state
  - geometric snap targets
- Need stable semantic selectors for every critical control path (you’ve started with `data-agent-id`, should be expanded).

### 11) Safety + Governance
- Need policy engine for risk levels (`safe`, `review`, `blocked`) per agent action.
- Need checkpoint templates (e.g., “before export,” “after quantity changes > X%”).
- Need operator diff/approval panel for proposed edits before commit.

### 12) Replay + Benchmarking
- Replay exists, but needs stronger reproducibility tools (seeded runs, deterministic snapshots, pass/fail checks).
- Need benchmark suite tied to real project scenarios and expected outcomes.

---

## High-Value “Do Next” Sequence (recommended)
1. **Project Integrity Center** (broken links + unscaled pages + orphans + fix actions).  
2. **Image/Page workflow parity pass** (overlay, repeating pages, multi-page actions).  
3. **Condition manager advanced ops** (bulk ops, renumber, conflict wizard, full usage graph).  
4. **Top-menu full wiring parity** (remove placeholders/disabled stubs, context states).  
5. **Agent safety/policy + dry-run mode**.  
6. **Then add the agent-readable integrity snapshot endpoint** (this will plug cleanly into #1).

If you want, I’ll start with #1 and #6 together so the integrity UI and agent endpoint are built as one system.

### 367. ASSISTANT

Reviewed your recording and extracted the main gaps still visible. Good news: core flow is running, but there are still parity-quality issues we should tighten next.

## What’s Working (confirmed in video)

- App boots and stays stable in Tauri with plans loaded.
- Conditions list, condition editing window, and takeoff drawing are functioning.
- Estimate summary loads and updates values.
- Integrity banner is visible in Estimate view.
- History panel and agent panel both render and respond.

## Highest-Impact Gaps Still Visible

- **Conditions panel density/alignment still off**
  - Row/action controls at the bottom (`Apply To Selection`, `Edit`, `Dup`, `Del`, `Renumber`, etc.) look cramped and partially clipped.
  - Table rhythm still not matching OST (header/body spacing and column alignment drift).

- **Condition Properties window still too compressed**
  - The dialog is still a narrow, long scroll region instead of an OST-style full usable property surface.
  - Field grouping is functional but not visually “native OST”.

- **Canvas interaction feedback is still ambiguous**
  - Crosshair + selected geometry + dashed overlay are visually busy in combination.
  - Hard to distinguish active edit mode vs selected/static state at a glance.

- **History panel content is too low-level/noisy**
  - Entries like `updateMarkup` / `moveVertex` are exposed raw.
  - Needs user-friendly labels and grouping (OST-style action history readability).

- **Top command surface still feels mixed-density**
  - Toolbar controls are present, but icon/button spacing and hierarchy still look hybrid rather than strict OST cadence.
  - “Activate Agent” button placement competes with history panel space.

- **Estimate view editing UX still rough**
  - Unit price edit behavior works, but row-level edit affordance feels inconsistent (some rows show `-`, some `0`, some `$` formatting shifts).
  - Revision compare is present but not yet presented as a clear workflow block.

- **Conditions-to-canvas linkage readability**
  - On-canvas geometry colors/styles update, but mapping condition row -> active markup is still not obvious enough in-session.

## Where We Should Continue Next (best ROI)

1. **Conditions panel + properties dialog polish pass** (layout/spacing/fixed columns/button rail)
2. **Canvas visual-state pass** (selection/edit/drawing states made unmistakable)
3. **History panel normalization** (human-readable action labels + grouping)
4. **Toolbar density harmonization** (strict OST spacing/priority)
5. **Estimate row edit consistency pass** (format + row behavior + revision block UX)

If you want, I’ll start immediately with item 1 and item 2 together (highest visible impact from this video), then send you a before/after checkpoint for that slice.

- **Track 6 (agent governance)**

    - `updatePageMetadata`

  - Additional conditions-panel density tuning and command-state consistency against OST cadence.
  - Command enablement in menu now references unified command gating in toolbar for core image/master actions.

- **Track 8 (release gate)**

## 25-Pass Visual Parity Audit

### Pass 1 — Shell/Layout
- Welcome modal still appears in app state paths where OST reference is already in active takeoff context.
- Left panel baseline width and internal padding are close but not locked to OST rhythm across states.

### Pass 2 — Top Menu Row
- Menu text spacing and hitbox width differ from OST in `File/Edit/View/...` row.
- Active menu dropdown style is slightly heavier/darker than OST.

### Pass 3 — Workspace Tabs
- `Projects / Takeoff / Summary / Estimate` tab vertical alignment is slightly off (baseline + top border rhythm).
- Active tab contrast and border weight differ from OST’s flatter look.

### Pass 4 — Command Strip Icons
- Icon cadence in tool strip is denser than OST (clustering around page/filter/zoom controls).
- Separator rhythm inconsistent (some tight, some wide).

### Pass 5 — Conditions Grid Header
- Column header balance (`No / Name / Formula / Q1 / Q2`) still not matching OST row density.
- Header text alignment and gutter sizes differ by a few pixels consistently.

### Pass 6 — Conditions Rows
- Row height + value wrapping differs; OST rows are cleaner with less vertical variance.
- Action cells (`Edit/Dup/Del`) still look appended rather than integrated to row rhythm.

### Pass 7 — Conditions Bottom Action Rail
- Rail currently over-stacked (bulk actions create visual clutter in compact space).
- OST reference shows simpler immediate-action rail with cleaner hierarchy.

### Pass 8 — Condition Properties Dialog
- Dialog still too “form-heavy” versus OST property-window feel.
- Tab section (`General/Advanced/Labor`) works, but spacing/field grouping still compressed.

### Pass 9 — Dialog Inputs/Typography
- Input widths vary too much by field; OST keeps tighter control width classes.
- Label-to-input spacing and line-height not yet uniform at every row.

### Pass 10 — Canvas Selection States
- Selected/editing/drawing visuals overlap too much (crosshair + dashed + handles).
- Need clearer state grammar: idle selection vs active edit vs in-progress draw.

### Pass 11 — Crosshair/Measurement Overlay
- Crosshair prominence is too dominant in some frames.
- OST reference keeps assistive overlays subtler unless actively drawing.

### Pass 12 — Geometry Stroke Language
- Stroke alpha/line cap/join differ from OST’s cleaner vector style.
- Multi-color condition overlays look more saturated than OST baseline.

### Pass 13 — Context Menu Behavior
- Context operations exist, but wording and option order don’t fully mirror OST workflow sequencing.
- Some context actions feel technical (`shape ops`) versus operator language.

### Pass 14 — Right-Side History Panel
- Panel content is too low-level (`addMarkup/updateMarkup`) and visually noisy.
- OST-like history should summarize intent-level actions with cleaner grouping.

### Pass 15 — Agent Panel Placement
- `Activate Agent` area competes with history panel area.
- OST parity mode should preserve takeoff-first visual priority and reduce right-top congestion.

### Pass 16 — Estimate Summary Header
- Header controls are functionally rich but visually denser than OST.
- Filter/export controls need stricter button width and spacing normalization.

### Pass 17 — Estimate Table Header Row
- Header text weight and row height slightly too heavy.
- Sticky header behavior is okay, but border and background tone mismatch OST.

### Pass 18 — Estimate Table Body
- Unit price edit cells still visually inconsistent (`-`, `0`, `$` mixed presentation).
- Numeric alignment and tabular rhythm need stricter formatting rules.

### Pass 19 — Traceability Cues
- Condition/page lineage is present, but discoverability in-row is still subtle.
- Drill-through affordance needs a clearer “jump” interaction pattern.

### Pass 20 — Page Workflow (QA/Overlay/Typical)
- Metadata exists, but on-screen affordances are not yet prominent enough for operator confidence.
- Page status badges need OST-style compact consistency.

### Pass 21 — Scrollbar/Viewport Feel
- Native scrollbar presence improved, but viewport feel still differs in motion smoothness and affordance hierarchy.
- Horizontal/vertical scrollbar prominence differs from OST references.

### Pass 22 — Visual Hierarchy (Global)
- Too many equally weighted controls in same horizontal bands.
- OST parity requires stronger tiering: primary workflow controls > secondary utilities.

### Pass 23 — Typography Pass
- Arial/size baseline mostly correct, but not fully normalized in all micro-surfaces.
- Tiny text controls still vary (10px/11px/12px inconsistently).

### Pass 24 — State Transitions
- Some state changes (select -> edit -> apply) feel abrupt without confirming UI cues.
- Need clearer transition signals matching OST’s calmer interaction tempo.

### Pass 25 — Overall Fidelity Readout
- Functional parity is much better.
- Visual parity is now **close in structure**, but not yet “highest possible” due to density/rhythm/state-language mismatches.

## Comprehensive Correction Backlog (What still needs to be corrected)

### A) High Priority (must-fix for “highest parity”)
1. Normalize conditions panel row/action rail architecture to OST spacing model.
2. Rebuild Condition Properties dialog into OST-style fixed-window proportions with strict field grid classes.
3. Simplify canvas visual-state grammar (selection/edit/draw overlays).
4. Convert history panel to intent-level action labels and grouped timeline.
5. Rebalance top command strip (icon spacing, separators, control tiers).
6. Unify estimate table formatting rules (currency, null, zero, alignment).

### B) Medium Priority
7. Tighten right-side utility panel composition (agent/history coexistence).
8. Strengthen traceability affordances (explicit jump links from estimate to markup/page).
9. Improve page-status display prominence (reviewed/verified/typical/overlay).
10. Normalize micro-typography and border weights app-wide.

### C) Lower Priority (final polish)
11. Refine transition cues between workflow states.
12. Match subtle color/alpha profile of strokes and helper overlays.
13. Improve scrollbar/viewport interaction polish to OST feel.

- Tighten table header/body rhythm to OST target.

- **Files**: `EstimatesView.tsx`, `estimateColumns.tsx`, `useEstimateData.ts`.

### Phase 5 — Final Pixel Convergence + Gate
- Run iterative screenshot diff loops against OST references.
- Apply micro-adjustments (font weight, padding, border alpha, control heights).
- Regression gates: build/lint + interaction smoke + parity checklist.
- **Files**: `AppLayout.tsx`, `Toolbar.tsx`, `Sidebar.tsx`, conditions/templates/estimates surfaces.

### 397. ASSISTANT

Yes — with your setup, a **black-box OST UI agent** is very feasible.

What we can do safely and legitimately:
- Automate OST the same way a human does: screen read -> click/type/hotkey -> verify result.
- Use your licensed local install only, without cracking, patching, or reverse-engineering OST internals.
- Build repeatable workflows (open project, select page, choose condition, perform takeoff, export/report).
- Keep human-in-the-loop controls so you can pause, approve, or take over instantly.

What we should **not** do:
- Parse or decompile proprietary binaries.
- Bypass license checks, anti-automation protections, or security controls.
- Depend on undocumented internal APIs from OST executables.

## Recommended Architecture (for your fixed device/screen)
- **Perception**: screenshot capture + OCR + icon/region matching for key UI elements.
- **Action layer**: deterministic mouse/keyboard commands (click, drag, double-click, hotkeys).
- **State machine**: explicit task states (Idle, Navigate, Draw, Verify, Recover, Complete).
- **Verification**: post-action checks (did line appear? did quantity update? did panel switch?).
- **Recovery**: if expected UI state not found, retry, backtrack, or ask for operator input.
- **Audit trail**: timestamped screenshots + action log + result log for each run.

## Why your constraints help
- Fixed screen size/resolution greatly improves reliability.
- Known OST version and stable layout reduce detection drift.
- Local-only execution is faster and more controllable.

## What I need from you to start building this
- OST version/build number.
- Confirm display settings will stay fixed (resolution + scaling %, e.g. 1920x1080 @ 100%).
- Preferred control mode: `safe` (approval gates) or `auto` (fully autonomous with checkpoints).
- 2-3 short recordings of exact workflows you want first (start with one: “create linear condition + takeoff + save/export”).
- Hotkey list you want the agent to use by default.
- A dedicated “test project” in OST we can safely automate.

If you want, next I can draft a **Phase 1 implementation plan** for an on-device OST agent prototype (first runnable milestone in 1 workflow).

### 410. USER

<user_query>
Would it make sense if I used a 60 inch display That would prevent or minimize the need to zoom in
</user_query>

### 411. ASSISTANT

It can help **you** visually, but for the **agent** it’s only beneficial if we keep pixel conditions stable.

Key point: screen *size* is less important than:
- fixed resolution,
- fixed scaling (`100%`),
- fixed OST window position/state.

A 60" display at low resolution can actually hurt OCR precision (text less crisp per pixel).  
For automation reliability, best setup is:

- native resolution (preferably high, e.g. 1440p/4K),
- Windows scaling locked at `100%`,
- OST always maximized on the same monitor,
- same theme/layout every run.

So yes, you can use 60", but only if we standardize the above. It may reduce your manual zooming, but agent workflows will still need zoom logic for fine geometry occasionally.

### 453. USER

<user_query>
Before I execute that is there an easier way to map the entire user interface That way the AI agent could just use logic When it comes to performing take offs can we map out some sort of ultra tight knit single pixel grid that would allow the agent to better manipulate the
</user_query>

### 454. ASSISTANT

Yes — and that’s the right question.

A pure “single-pixel grid map of everything” is possible, but it’s usually too brittle (tiny UI shifts break it).  
The **easier + stronger** approach is a **hybrid UI map**:

- **Layer 1: Stable anchors**  
  Fixed landmarks (top menus, left panel tabs, Boost header, Run button zone, page canvas bounds).

- **Layer 2: Relative regions**  
  Define controls relative to anchors (ex: Run button = bottom-right of Boost dialog), not absolute pixels only.

- **Layer 3: Visual signatures**  
  For each important target, store color/shape templates (button blue, warning banner, checkbox glyph).

- **Layer 4: Action graph (logic)**  
  A state machine: `OpenBoost -> Preflight -> SetOptions -> Run -> Verify`, with retries and fallbacks.

- **Layer 5: Verification contracts**  
  “Success means X changed” (dialog disappeared, warning absent, counts updated), not just “click happened.”

So yes, we can “map the interface,” but do it as a **structured control map**, not a raw pixel lattice.

## Recommendation
Build a **UI Atlas file** (JSON) for OST:
- monitor bounds
- anchors
- relative controls
- detection thresholds
- per-step expected states

Then the agent uses logic against that atlas.

If you want, I can implement this next as:
- `scripts/ost_ui_atlas.json`
- `scripts/ost_ui_mapper.py` (capture anchors/templates)
- integrate atlas lookup into `ost_boost_agent.py` so clicks become anchor-relative automatically.

### 596. ASSISTANT

## Full Maverick Plan

Here’s the rest of the plan end-to-end, in order:

1. **Startup State Machine (Paintbrush first, Maverick last)**
- One orchestrated boot path.
- Dependencies start in fixed sequence with readiness checks.
- Maverick stays offline until all services are healthy.
- Single-instance guard prevents duplicate watcher stacks.

2. **Always-On Watchdog + Auto-Recovery**
- Continuous health monitoring.
- If any dependency fails, restart dependency first.
- Maverick only resumes after dependency health is restored.
- Timeout/retry policies avoid partial or hung startup.

3. **Maverick Runtime Controller**
- Central runtime wrapper for all agent actions.
- Every action follows: `intent -> plan -> execute -> verify -> log -> summarize`.
- One instrumented dispatcher so nothing runs “off the books.”

4. **Step-by-Step Logging + Failure Intelligence**
- Append-only per-session/per-project logs.
- Every step logs expected vs observed outcome.
- Failures log root-cause hypothesis, retries, and resolution path.
- Structured outputs: detailed log, failure index, human-readable session summary.

5. **Conversation Memory + “Since Last Time” Reports**
- Persist conversation and operation milestones by project/session.
- Delta summaries when you ask what changed since last discussion.
- Report includes: completed work, unresolved blockers, risks, recommended next actions.

6. **10-Failure Coaching Trigger (Your Rule)**
- Failure counter per task type.
- Only after **10 failed attempts**:
  - Maverick asks you targeted usage questions,
  - records guided clicks/context for that workflow,
  - stores correction as reusable playbook.
- Cooldown prevents repeated nagging on the same solved issue.

7. **Estimator Quality Layer (Painting/Finishes Focus)**
- Uses scope docs, schedules, unit matrix signals, and conflict detection.
- Pre-completion quality checks for coverage/completeness and quantity anomalies.
- Session report marks pass/warn/fail with reasons.

8. **Self-Update Policy (Your Choice: Suggest-Only)**
- Maverick can learn and propose improvements.
- Maverick **does not auto-apply** code/config/runtime changes.
- Proposed updates go to approval queue with risk + rollback notes.

## Definition of Done
- Paintbrush starts automatically in order every time.
- Maverick only activates after dependency health gate passes.
- Full step/failure/resolution trace exists for every run.
- “What changed since last time?” works accurately.
- Coaching/click capture only starts after 10 failures.
- No duplicate runtime stacks.
- No self-modification without your explicit approval.

If you want, I can now switch from planning to implementation and execute this in that same order.

### 617. ASSISTANT

You caught a **logging clarity issue**, not a root-path bug.

What was happening:
- Maverick **is** watching `G:\Shared drives\SKYLINE 2026\AI Bids` (correct root).

- So behavior was correct, but the message looked misleading.

I updated it so it now prints:
- `watch_root=G:\Shared drives\SKYLINE 2026\AI Bids`
- `project_scan_count=...`
- `Processing project under watch_root: ...`

So you can clearly see it is monitoring `AI Bids` first, then processing child folders.

## Detailed Next Plan (Maverick vNext)

### Objective
Move Maverick from “operational and stable” to “high-confidence autonomous estimator assistant” by:
1. improving conflict confidence quality,
2. reducing quantity/runtime variance,
3. adding project-level reporting and execution discipline,
4. hardening startup and recovery behavior.

---

## Phase 1 — Confidence Pipeline Completion

### 1.1 Target timed-out projects automatically
- Build a retry queue for projects that previously timed out in scope intel/profile.
- Use adaptive limits (`max-files`, `max-pdf-pages`) by project size.
- Persist queue state and retry attempts.

### 1.2 Enrich conflict confidence signals
- Add cross-source corroboration scoring:
  - schedule + specs + plans alignment boosts confidence.
- Penalize single-source or OCR-noisy-only conflicts.
- Keep dedupe but add provenance summaries (which files supported each conflict).

### 1.3 Quality output upgrade
- In `quality-gates`, split:
  - `actionable_conflicts`,
  - `needs_more_evidence`,
  - `informational_conflicts`.

**Acceptance**
- No project remains “silent-timeout” without retry metadata.
- Conflict confidence fields populate meaningfully (non-zero high/medium where warranted).
- Quality report can clearly explain why a conflict is actionable.

---

## Phase 2 — Variance Reduction Loop

### 2.1 Archetype-specific stabilization policies
- Add per-archetype retry profiles for:
  - `boost-run-click`,
  - `boost-open-dialog`,
  - `setup-focus-window`,
  - `setup-missing-anchor`.

### 2.2 Adaptive wait/retry tuning
- Increase/decrease waits/retries based on recent failure streaks.
- Add caps and cooldown to avoid runaway retry loops.

### 2.3 Variance diagnostics in report
- Add top contributors to quantity/runtime variance:
  - module id,
  - attempt window,
  - last known failure reason.

**Acceptance**
- Estimator QA trends improve from `warn` toward `pass`.
- Daily report identifies exactly what is driving variance.

---

## Phase 3 — Project-Scoped Reporting

### 3.1 Per-project artifacts
- Generate report files per project key:
  - `output/maverick/project_reports/<project>/daily_report.md`
  - `.../daily_report.json`
- Keep `_global` aggregate report.

### 3.2 Delta intelligence
- Maintain per-project snapshot cursor.
- Show “new since last report” deltas by project, not just global.

### 3.3 Action prioritization
- Top actions ranked by:
  1. blocker severity,
  2. expected estimator impact,
  3. confidence score.

**Acceptance**
- Every active project has an independent report artifact.
- Delta section accurately tracks project-local changes.

---

## Phase 4 — Recovery Playbooks and Auto-Resolution

### 4.1 Recovery playbook registry
- Formalize playbook metadata:
  - trigger condition,
  - execution steps,
  - success criteria,
  - rollback/fallback.

### 4.2 Playbook effectiveness tracking
- Log playbook hit rate and success rate per archetype.
- If a playbook repeatedly fails, escalate to coach mode faster.

### 4.3 Coach lifecycle hygiene
- Auto-resolve stale pending coach requests when success conditions are met.
- Suppress duplicate coach prompts for recently-resolved archetypes.

**Acceptance**
- Fewer recurring unresolved coach requests.
- Failure trends include “playbook attempted” and outcome.

---

## Phase 5 — Startup + Operational Hardening

### 5.1 Startup confidence pack
- On boot, persist:
  - lock health,
  - dependency order evidence,
  - readiness timings,
  - immediate blocker count.

### 5.2 Single-instance enforcement audit
- Add periodic assertion: exactly one Maverick runtime tree.
- Auto-remediate duplicates if detected.

### 5.3 Fast operator health command
- One command gives:
  - startup status,
  - blockers,
  - trends,
  - quality,
  - estimator QA.

**Acceptance**
- Boot verification artifact created every startup.
- No duplicate watcher/runtime stacks in steady state.

## What’s now built

- **Batch protocol builder intake**
  - `protocol-builder-intake`
  - Analyzes selected projects/plans and produces:

  - `protocol-verify` (approve/reject)
  - `protocol-status` (per project)

- **Run gating**
  - `run-module` now checks protocol verification first and blocks start if not verified (unless explicitly overridden).

## Commands you can use

- Build intake questions for a batch:
  - `python "scripts/ost_orchestrator.py" protocol-builder-intake --project-ids "TP-0001,TP-0002,TP-0003,TP-0004" --registry "scripts/ost_training_registry.json"`

  - `python "scripts/ost_orchestrator.py" protocol-prepare-batch --project-ids "TP-0001,TP-0002,TP-0003,TP-0004" --registry "scripts/ost_training_registry.json"`

- Verify protocol before runs:
  - `python "scripts/ost_orchestrator.py" protocol-verify --protocol-id "PROTO-general-20260402_222250" --approved --verifier "travi" --notes "approved for this batch"`

- Check project protocol status:
  - `python "scripts/ost_orchestrator.py" protocol-status --project-id TP-0001`

### 772. USER

<user_query>
What would be the best way for you to identify the shapes of the rooms on the plans That way you can increase your accuracy
</user_query>

### 773. ASSISTANT

Best way is a **hybrid approach**: use plan geometry from the PDF + on-screen visual cues from OST + your corrections as feedback.

## What works best

- **Parse room boundaries from the source PDF first** (vector lines if available, OCR + line detection if raster) so I’m not guessing from screenshots alone.
- **Detect enclosed polygons** (rooms) from wall lines, then score each polygon as “likely room” based on size, closure, wall thickness, and label proximity.
- **Read room labels/text** inside or near polygons (`Bedroom`, `Bath`, unit IDs, etc.) and map those to your condition rules.
- **Register PDF coordinates to OST screen coordinates** so clicks land in the exact room shape (not rough center-point guesses).
- **Use your highlighted example as ground truth** for that page and compare my traced polygon vs your polygon overlap (IoU/coverage %). If low, auto-undo.
- **Learn from corrections**: every undo/retry updates a per-project shape model (what wall types, offsets, and room label patterns you actually use).

## Why this is better than current clicks

Right now I’m largely selecting candidates by visual grouping and OCR fragments.  
To increase accuracy materially, I need **explicit room polygons** and **page coordinate alignment** so takeoffs are geometry-driven, not just “best-looking box.”

## Practical implementation path

- Add a `room-shape profiler` step:
  1) ingest plan page  
  2) extract wall graph  
  3) build enclosed room polygons  
  4) attach room labels  
  5) export clickable room centers + boundaries
- Add a `match gate` before committing takeoff:
  - if polygon overlap with example < threshold, mark bad work + auto-erase
- Store accepted polygons as reusable templates per unit type/protocol.

If you want, I can build this as the next module so Maverick traces **actual room shapes** before takeoff instead of relying on grouping heuristics.

### 774. USER

<user_query>
That is going to turn into a lot of different Polygon shapes because there are so many different types of rooms would it be easier for you to look for patterns for instance perimeter walls are usually dark Gray or black and the thickness of the line is consistent. The outer perimeter walls tend to be thicker the interior walls are just slightly thinner in terms of the line thickness There's also other types of walls that will have a cross pattern and those are typically CMU walls. While you are analyzing plans You should very specific items and then keep a database by item type That way it's easier for you analyze what you are looking at while you are completing a takeoff
</user_query>

### 775. ASSISTANT

Yes — that is a better direction for your workflow than trying to memorize every room polygon upfront.

## Better strategy: pattern-first, item-type database

- **Detect wall classes by visual signature** instead of room shape catalog:
  - perimeter walls: darker, thicker, consistent stroke
  - interior partitions: slightly thinner
  - CMU walls: hatch/cross pattern texture
- **Segment by item type first** (wall system, not room identity), then infer room boundaries from those systems only when needed.
- **Build a feature database by item type** so Maverick learns reusable rules:
  - `item_type`: perimeter_wall / interior_wall / cmu_wall / door / frame / etc.
  - `features`: line thickness range, grayscale range, texture score, hatch presence, continuity
  - `context`: sheet type, scale, project type, unit type
  - `confidence + corrections`: accepted/rejected by you

## Why this fits your training goals

- More stable across projects than room-by-room polygons
- Easier to coach (“this is CMU”, “this is perimeter”) than redrawing every room
- Lets Maverick reason like an estimator: classify scope elements first, then apply takeoff rules

## How I’d implement it next

1. Add a **plan feature extractor** for line thickness, intensity, and hatch texture.  
2. Add an **item-type knowledge store** (JSON/SQLite) with per-type signatures and confidence.  
3. Add a **classification pass** before any takeoff action.  
4. Apply your existing cleanup guard: if classification confidence is low or mismatch detected, auto-undo bad work.  
5. Log “what I saw + why I classified it” per action for coaching.

If you want, I can start implementing this now as a new module (`item_type_classifier`) and wire it into the current training run path.

### 820. USER

<user_query>
On-Screen Takeoff (OST) from ConstructConnect (formerly On Center Software) supports extensive keyboard shortcuts in version 4.0 and later (current releases build on the same core shortcuts with minor enhancements). These apply primarily on Windows and are documented in the official user guide/help system.
The most comprehensive lists appear in the help articles for general keyboard shortcuts and Takeoff Tab/Takeoff Window specifics. Many shortcuts are context-sensitive (e.g., they behave differently depending on whether focus is in the image window, conditions list, or a dialog). Some require the numeric keypad for zoom functions.
General/Program-Wide Keyboard Shortcuts (from OST help article 01.03.01)
These work across much of the application:

Ctrl + A: Select All (selects all objects on the current page or window)
Ctrl + C: Copy (copies selection to clipboard)
Ctrl + D: Duplicate (duplicates selected Bid, Condition, or Master table record; context varies in newer versions for takeoff objects)
Ctrl + G: Go To (opens dialog to enter a specific page number on the Takeoff Tab)
Ctrl + I: Opens the Adjust Images dialog box (Takeoff Tab)
Ctrl + L: Shows/Hides the Layers dockbar (Takeoff Tab)
Ctrl + O: Open (opens the Open Databases dialog)
Ctrl + P: Print (opens Print or Print Preview)
Ctrl + R: Activates Rotate Takeoff controls (takeoff only, not the image; Takeoff Tab)
Ctrl + S: Activates Spin Takeoff control (takeoff only, not the image; Takeoff Tab)
Ctrl + T: Opens Set Takeoff Area dialog (when using a digitizer; Takeoff Tab)
Ctrl + V: Paste
Ctrl + X: Cut (moves selection)
Ctrl + Y: Redo (reverses Undo)
Ctrl + Z: Undo (reverses previous action)
Alt: Activates menus (with underlined letter) or Panning function on Takeoff Tab
Alt + Mouse drag: Pans the plan on the Takeoff Tab
Page Up: Previous plan page/image
Page Down: Next plan page/image
Ctrl + Page Up: Previous Condition (in Conditions Properties)
Ctrl + Page Down: Next Condition (in Conditions Properties)
Insert: Adds new record (Database, Bid, Condition, etc., depending on active area)
Ctrl + Enter: Accepts and closes current dialog box
Esc: Dismisses dialog or cancels command
Spacebar: Toggles between Takeoff and Select tools (Takeoff Tab)
Ctrl + 2: Opens/closes the Annotation and View Window (secondary view for other pages/annotations)
Shift (during takeoff): Temporarily overrides Snap To settings for Linear/Area conditions
***** (asterisk, preferably numeric keypad): Zooms to full page (Image Window) or expands collapsed groupings in lists
+ (plus, preferably numeric keypad): Zooms in or expands grouping
- (minus, preferably numeric keypad): Zooms out or collapses grouping
/ (forward slash, preferably numeric keypad): Zooms to 100%

Function Keys

F1: Context-sensitive help
F2: Edit mode (field or cell)
F4: Opens/closes drop-down or lookup
F9: Refreshes Takeoff Totals (sends info to linked pricing app)

Mouse/Scroll Wheel Functions

Scroll Wheel: Pans vertically (or cycles pages if over Pages dropdown)
Ctrl + Scroll: Zooms in/out
Shift + Scroll: Pans horizontally

A printable keyboard shortcut card (v5) is referenced in the help: https://downloads.oncenter.com/Downloads/OST/OST_Keyboard_Shortcut_Card_v5.jpg (this is an image; it summarizes many of the above).
Takeoff Tab / Takeoff Window Specific Shortcuts
These are especially useful during measuring/markup (focus on the Takeoff Window/Image):

Spacebar: Toggle between Selection Tool and last-used Takeoff Tool
Delete (Del): Deletes selected takeoff object(s) or annotation
Ctrl + M: Activates Magnifier Tool (magnifies a region without changing overall zoom; toggle off by selecting another tool)
Ctrl + S: Split a linear or area segment (hold and click on the segment)
A (during linear/area drawing): Creates an arc (3-point oval section)
R (during linear/area drawing): Creates a round (3-point circle section)
Home: First page in the bid
End: Last page in the bid
Ctrl + click and drag: Alternative magnifier/zoom region
Alt + click and drag: Pan tool

Additional notes on duplication (Ctrl + D) in takeoff context:

Single press: Duplicates objects offset down/right.
Hold Ctrl + D: Enters "Duplicate at Click" mode (click to place).

Zoom/navigation (numeric keypad preferred for +/-/ */ /):

+: Zoom in
-: Zoom out
*****: Zoom to full page/fit
/: Zoom to 100%

Page navigation with mouse scroll wheel also works in various modes (e.g., with modifiers for pan/zoom).
Additional Tips and Version Notes

Version 4.0+ specifics: OST 4.0 (released around 2016 with ongoing updates through 2026) retains these core shortcuts while adding features like improved Takeoff Boost, right-click reassignment of conditions, and second-view annotations. Newer releases (including ConstructConnect-branded updates) may have slight expansions or context changes, but the lists above cover the foundation for v4.0 and better. Check Help > Keyboard Shortcuts or the user guide within the software for any version-specific additions.
Shortcuts are most effective with focus in the correct pane (e.g., image window for zoom/takeoff tools).
Overlays or advanced features may have community/AHK workarounds (e.g., Ctrl + W for import in some setups), but these are not official core commands.
For full details or updates, open the built-in help in OST (F1 or menu) and search for "keyboard shortcuts," or visit the ConstructConnect help site (help.constructconnect.com) under On-Screen Takeoff User Guide > Introduction.

If your installed version shows differences or you need shortcuts for a specific tool (e.g., overlays, digitizer), provide more details for refinement. The printable card image is a quick reference if you can access the download link.
</user_query>

### 821. ASSISTANT

Perfect — this is exactly the right reference, and I’ll use it as the control map going forward.

For Maverick training in OST, I’ll prioritize these in this order:

- `Ctrl + A` then `Delete` to clear page takeoff work
- `Esc` to cancel/exit tool states before and after actions
- `Spacebar` to toggle Select/Takeoff tool safely
- `Ctrl + Z` / `Ctrl + Y` only as fallback recovery
- `Page Up` / `Page Down` and `Ctrl + G` for deterministic navigation
- `Ctrl + Scroll` and keypad zoom shortcuts for stable framing during pattern matching

This is a good protocol baseline for reducing UI misses and improving repeatability. I’ll keep this as the standard behavior set while we continue training.

### 891. ASSISTANT

Because the run is **executing**, but it’s failing the final match gates.

In the latest full run (`boost_then_copy_attempt_TP-0001_20260403_012142.json`):

- It **did select a condition** (`selected_condition_qty: 2.0`)
- It **did draw a takeoff stroke** (`stroke_points` were recorded)
- But the copied result scored only **35.61** vs required **55**
- And classifier confidence was **0.3751** vs required **0.5**

So it’s not stopping early; it’s completing the flow and then being marked bad because the output doesn’t match Boost closely enough.

Most likely root causes right now:
- Condition OCR finds an active row, but not always the *same intended condition type* as Boost.
- The left-target candidate can still be semantically wrong (it picked a candidate labeled like `atte` in that run), so the stroke lands in the wrong object family.

If you want, next I’ll harden this by forcing condition/target agreement with the Boost snapshot (same candidate class and region neighborhood) before the stroke is allowed.

there is an excellent official resource that does a comprehensive job of explaining On-Screen Takeoff (OST, by ConstructConnect/On Center Software) and all its screens, tabs, and features—though no single “all-in-one” diagram of every screen was found.

Key sections from the User Guide (full TOC)

01 Introduction to On-Screen Takeoff → User interface overview and basics.

Direct link to the full User Guide: https://help.constructconnect.com/on-screen-takeoff-user-guide-68
Additional excellent supporting resources

Getting Started with On-Screen Takeoff® (quick-start series + full overview): https://help.constructconnect.com/getting-started-with-on-screen-takeoff-112 — includes a “Create Your First Takeoff in Under 5 Minutes” guide.

YouTube series like “On-Screen Takeoff – Getting Started” (overview of main tabs: Projects, Takeoff, Summary, Estimate) and beginner tutorials that visually walk through the full workflow.

The User Guide and videos together give you everything you need—no single static diagram exists that maps every screen and feature at once (based on extensive searches), but the structured documentation and visual training materials do an outstanding job of covering the complete software.
If you have access to OST, the built-in Help (F1) also points directly to these same resources. Let me know if you’d like links to specific sections (e.g., Takeoff Tab details) or help finding a particular feature!

### 959. ASSISTANT

Found it — you likely mean **Zhipu AI GLM-OCR**.

Best official references:
- [Zhipu GLM-OCR docs](https://zhipu-32152247.mintlify.app/guides/vlm/glm-ocr)
- [GLM-OCR GitHub](https://github.com/zai-org/GLM-OCR)
- [Hugging Face model page](https://hf.co/zai-org/GLM-OCR)

Quick take:
- It’s a lightweight OCR/document model (~0.9B) for PDFs/images.
- Good for complex layouts (tables, mixed content, forms, receipts, stamps).
- Outputs structured text/markdown (useful for downstream parsing rules).

For your OST workflow, this is useful for:
- Better condition-list OCR (reduce `ceiling`/`gwb` misreads)
- Better pre-click verification text extraction
- Better post-attempt comparison notes

If you want, next step I can wire a **GLM-OCR fallback path**: use current local OCR first, and auto-call GLM-OCR only when confidence is low or keyword matching fails.

## README

### Short Description
`Paintbrush.pro` is an OST automation and training workspace for Maverick. It focuses on screenshot-first analysis, condition-aware takeoff attempts, and iterative quality validation to improve match accuracy against reference takeoffs.

### GitHub Setup
1. Create a new GitHub repository.
2. From project root, initialize and push:

```bash
git init
git add .
git commit -m "Initial project import"
git branch -M main
git remote add origin https://github.com/<your-user>/<your-repo>.git
git push -u origin main
```

### Local Prerequisites
- Python 3.10+
- Node.js (if using frontend/dev scripts)
- Windows environment for OST UI automation
- Tesseract installed (fallback OCR path)

### Environment Variables
Create `.env.txt` (or `.env`) with keys as needed:

```env
# xAI / Grok
GROK_[REDACTED]
GROK_MODEL=grok-4.20-0309-reasoning

# Optional GitHub Models path
GITHUB_[REDACTED]
```

```bash
python scripts/grok_live_bridge.py --mode xai --env-file ".env.txt"
```

Use `/exit` to stop.

### Notes
- Do not commit real API keys.
- Keep secrets in ignored local env files.
- Use GitHub branches/PRs for major workflow changes.

### 1003. ASSISTANT

Maverick for `Paintbrush.pro` is an automation and training system for On-Screen Takeoff (OST) that learns a user’s estimating style and continuously improves takeoff accuracy through a Boost -> Analyze -> Copy feedback loop. It combines desktop UI automation, screenshot-based computer vision, OCR-driven condition selection, item-type pattern classification (perimeter/interior/CMU walls and related elements), strict match gates, and self-review telemetry to reduce bad work and improve repeatability across attempts. The project includes protocol-aware workflows, cleanup and unblock safeguards, condition verification logic, and detailed JSON/Markdown reporting so training outcomes can be measured, compared, and refined over time.

### 1010. ASSISTANT

Done — I implemented an automatic mouse takeover pause so this won’t keep fighting your control.

What I changed:

- Added shared guard module: `scripts/mouse_takeover_guard.py`
- Integrated it into all automation scripts that can drive mouse/keyboard:
  - `scripts/ost_left_blank_takeoff_attempt.py`
  - `scripts/ost_condition_takeoff_attempt.py`
  - `scripts/ost_select_condition_row.py`
  - `scripts/ost_grouping_selector.py`
  - `scripts/ost_boost_agent.py`
  - `scripts/ost_undo_actions.py`
  - `scripts/ost_project_setup_agent.py`
  - `scripts/ost_ui_mapper.py`

How it behaves now:

- Before any automation click/move/keypress, it checks for manual mouse movement.
- If you took control (movement above threshold), automation pauses for **15 seconds** automatically.
- Then it resumes safely.
- It logs when triggered, e.g. `mouse_takeover_detected pause_s=15.0 ...`.

Defaults (can be tuned with env vars):

- `MAVERICK_MOUSE_TAKEOVER_PAUSE_S=15`
- `MAVERICK_MOUSE_TAKEOVER_THRESHOLD_PX=12`
- `MAVERICK_MOUSE_TAKEOVER_GRACE_S=0.8`
- `MAVERICK_MOUSE_TAKEOVER_GUARD_ENABLED=true`

Also verified:

- No OST automation processes are running right now (`no_ost_automation_running`).

### 1012. ASSISTANT

Maverick for Paintbrush.pro is an OST automation and training system designed to learn and replicate estimator takeoff style with high consistency. It uses a screenshot-first workflow (Boost -> Analyze -> Copy), OCR-driven condition detection, visual item-type classification (such as perimeter/interior/CMU wall signatures), strict match/verification gates, and self-review telemetry to reduce bad work and improve repeatability over time. The project includes robust runtime safeguards for real-world desktop operation, including automatic UI unblock handling, cleanup controls, taskbar-safe interactions, and a mouse-takeover guard that pauses automation when the user takes control. It also supports Grok-assisted troubleshooting and structured reporting so performance can be measured, compared, and continuously improved across training blocks.

### 1036. ASSISTANT

You’ll need a **Z.ai / Zhipu developer API key** for the GLM endpoint.

## Get a GLM API key

1. Create/sign in to your Zhipu developer account (Z.ai / BigModel platform).
2. Open the API Keys section in the developer console.
3. Create a new key (name it like `paintbrush-ocr-prod`).
4. Copy it once and store it safely.

## Add it locally (PowerShell)

For current terminal session only:

```powershell
$env:GLMOCR_API_KEY="your_new_key_here"
```

Persistent for your user (new terminals):

```powershell
setx GLMOCR_API_KEY "your_new_key_here"
```

Then restart terminal/Cursor to pick up `setx` vars.

## Quick verify

I can run this after you set it:

```powershell
python -c "import numpy as np, cv2, json; from scripts.ocr_engine import create_ocr_engine; img=np.full((80,320,3),255,dtype=np.uint8); cv2.putText(img,'Takeoff 123',(10,50),cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX,1.0,(0,0,0),2,cv2.LINE_AA); o=create_ocr_engine('scripts/ocr_engine.config.json'); r=o.ocr_text(img, context='Extract visible text exactly.'); print(json.dumps({'engine_used':r.get('engine_used'),'fallback_used':r.get('fallback_used'),'reason':r.get('fallback_reason'),'text':r.get('text')}, indent=2))"
```

You want:
- `engine_used: "glmocr"`
- `fallback_used: false`

If getting a new provider key is a hassle right now, we can keep using your current xAI path and I can switch defaults back to that immediately.

## Paste-ready prompt (for Cursor chat with screenshots)

```text
You are a UI perception and action planner for On-Screen Takeoff (OST).

Task:
1) Detect key UI elements from the screenshot:
   - Conditions panel
   - active condition rows (qty > 0)
   - Boost button
   - Run Boost button
   - page navigation
   - likely “Takeoff” controls
2) Return bounding boxes and center coordinates.
3) Propose safest click sequence to perform: Boost -> verify populated -> select active ceiling/GWB condition -> start takeoff in matching area.
4) If an element is missing, provide fallback strategy and next-best target.

Output JSON only:
{
  "elements":[{"label":"","bbox":[x,y,w,h],"center":[x,y],"confidence":0.0}],
  "active_conditions":[{"name":"","qty":0.0,"center":[x,y],"confidence":0.0}],
  "click_plan":[{"step":1,"target_label":"","coords":[x,y],"why":"","confidence":0.0}],
  "fallbacks":[{"if":"","then":""}]
}
```

- `api_style`: `openai_chat_completions`

  - `https://api.z.ai/api/paas/v4`  
  - or `https://api.z.ai/api/coding/paas/v4`
- `model`: `glm-4.6v` (or your available vision model)
- optional fallbacks: `glm-4v`, `glm-4.7`
- `fallback_to_tesseract: true`

## 4) Run a smoke test
From project root:

```powershell
python -c "import numpy as np, cv2, json; from scripts.ocr_engine import create_ocr_engine; img=np.full((80,320,3),255,dtype=np.uint8); cv2.putText(img,'Takeoff 123',(10,50),cv2.FONT_HERSHEY_SIMPLEX,1.0,(0,0,0),2,cv2.LINE_AA); o=create_ocr_engine('scripts/ocr_engine.config.json'); r=o.ocr_text(img, context='Extract visible text exactly.'); print(json.dumps({'engine_used':r.get('engine_used'),'fallback_used':r.get('fallback_used'),'reason':r.get('fallback_reason'),'text':r.get('text')}, indent=2))"
```

Expected success:
- `engine_used: "glmocr"`
- `fallback_used: false`

If you get `401`:
- key invalid/missing or wrong account scope

If `404`:
- endpoint/model mismatch (switch `/paas/v4` vs `/coding/paas/v4`, or model name)

If you want, after you set the key, say `retest now` and I’ll run/verify it for you immediately.

### 1111. USER

<user_query>
Or would it be better to Design a plan that would expedite the learning process Now that we have better eyeballs
</user_query>

### 1112. ASSISTANT

Yes — **that’s the better move right now**.

Now that GLM vision is working, the fastest path is a **short, tight learning plan** instead of brute-force attempts.

## Accelerated Learning Plan (with “better eyeballs”)

1. **Stabilize one golden loop first**
- Workflow: `Boost -> wait/verify -> snapshot -> erase -> copy`
- Use **one page**, **one condition family** (ceiling/GWB), **one attempt style**
- Goal: remove variability before scaling

2. **Create a “teacher target” artifact per attempt**
- Save:
  - boost snapshot
  - selected condition row + qty
  - target region bbox/center
  - first click point + stroke path
- This becomes the ground-truth that the copy attempt must match

3. **Two-stage OCR strategy**
- Keep fast local scan for row discovery
- Use GLM only for high-value reads (target verification + ambiguous labels)
- This gives speed + better perception where it matters

4. **Hard gates before drawing**
- Don’t draw unless all pass:
  - active condition found (qty > 0)
  - not unassigned
  - target in expected boost region
  - item-type match confidence above threshold
- If any fail: auto-adjust and retry, no blind clicks

5. **Micro-batch learning cadence**
- Run in blocks of **5 attempts**
- After each block:
  - apply 1 concrete adjustment from self-review
  - rerun next block
- Don’t do long 20+ blocks until 2 consecutive 5-blocks improve

6. **Success criteria to unlock scale**
- Condition verification pass rate >= 80%
- Match score median improving block-over-block
- Bad-work rate trending down for 2 blocks
- Then expand to 10, then 20 attempts

## Why this is faster
- You learn from clean, comparable data
- Fewer wasted attempts
- GLM vision is used where it gives leverage, not everywhere

If you want, I’ll implement this as a **new “accelerated-learning” run profile** in the orchestrator and start the first 5-attempt teaching block immediately.

- Runtime safety/mutex expectations.
- Acceptance gates (condition lock rate, quantity corruption prevention, geometry trend).

This directly addresses your point that the condition cannot be expected to behave like Boost after erase.

### What I implemented now

- Added `scripts/ost_condition_style_inspector.py`
  - Opens the selected condition (double-click row),
  - OCR-reads the dialog for `Style` (`area`, `linear`, `count`, `attachment`),
  - closes dialog (`Esc`) and returns structured JSON.

- Wired style inspection into `scripts/ost_left_blank_takeoff_attempt.py`
  - After condition lock, Maverick now runs style inspection.
  - Stores:
    - `condition_style`
    - `condition_style_inspection`
  - Uses style to choose behavior:
    - `area` → polygon-style clicks
    - `linear` → path-style clicks (single clicks with double-click termination behavior pattern)
    - `count` → point/count behavior

### Your condition point (critical) is now reflected

You are correct: this should be based on the **condition itself**, not “tool behavior.”  
The flow is now:

1. Lock condition identity (`ceiling`/`gwb`, row).
2. Open condition.
3. Read style.
4. Close condition.
5. Execute takeoff using style-specific click logic.

What it does on trigger:

- Force-stops active Python automation processes for this workspace (Maverick/OST scripts)
- Uses a short cooldown to avoid repeated accidental triggers

Useful commands:
- Start watcher:
  - `python "scripts/ost_emergency_pause_hotkey.py" watch --window-ms 1200 --poll-ms 30 --cooldown-ms 1800`
- Pause immediately (manual test):
  - `python "scripts/ost_emergency_pause_hotkey.py" pause-now`
- Clear pause flag:
  - `python "scripts/ost_emergency_pause_hotkey.py" clear`

### 1277. ASSISTANT

From prior Grok-aligned feedback in this project, the stance is basically:

- **Safety gates first, then training**: hard stop controls + window-bound actions before more autonomous retries.
- **Deterministic phase gating**: fail fast on condition lock/style mismatch instead of “try anyway.”
- **Evidence-driven loop**: every attempt should produce artifacts (selection evidence, geometry match, OCR telemetry, reason-coded failure).
- **Narrow scope for reliability**: keep Phase 1 constrained (`area`, `ceiling/gwb`) until consistency is proven.
- **Success should be streak-based**: your selected target of **3 consecutive successful runs** is the right milestone before expansion.

So Grok would likely support the roundtable plan we just set:  
**stabilize controls -> run a tight two-reference replay lane -> require 3 in a row -> then widen scope.**

If you want, I can draft the exact “question payload” we’d send to Grok for a final tie-breaker opinion at the start of our planning meeting.
